Video clip</div></div></div>
<p>There are 850 northern bald ibises in European zoos and a further 250 in captivity in Japan and North America.<sup id="cite_ref-IAGNBI2003_61-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IAGNBI2003-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The 49 European zoos keeping this species produce 80 to 100 young birds per year, and earlier attempts at releasing captive-bred birds included close to 150 birds between 1976 and 1986 from an aviary at Birecik, 75 from <a href="/wiki/Tel_Aviv" title="Tel Aviv">Tel Aviv</a> Zoo in 1983, and an unspecified number from a project in <a href="/wiki/Almer%C3%ADa" title="Almería">Almería</a>, Spain, from 1991 to 1994; all these attempts were unsuccessful.<sup id="cite_ref-waza2_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza2-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> All northern bald ibises in zoos, other than those in Turkey, are of the western population, and were imported from Morocco. Three bloodlines exist; the earliest relates to importations to <a href="/wiki/Zoo_Basel" class="mw-redirect" title="Zoo Basel">Zoo Basel</a>, Switzerland in the 1950s and 1960s, the next is the descendants of birds taken in the 1970s to stock <a href="/wiki/Rabat" title="Rabat">Rabat</a> Zoo, and the last captured wild birds were those taken to the Naturzoo, <a href="/wiki/Rheine" title="Rheine">Rheine</a>, in 1976 and 1978.<sup id="cite_ref-waza_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Captive birds have a high incidence of skin problems, and 40% of those birds that had to be put down suffered from chronic ulcerative <a href="/wiki/Dermatitis" title="Dermatitis">dermatitis</a>, characterised by feather loss, rawness, and ulceration on the back, neck, and the undersides of the wings. The cause of this disease is unknown.<sup id="cite_ref-Quevedo_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Quevedo-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> Other major disease problems reported in zoo collections have been avian <a href="/wiki/Tuberculosis" title="Tuberculosis">tuberculosis</a>, gastric foreign bodies, bone disease, and heart problems.<sup id="cite_ref-greenwood_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-greenwood-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> An outbreak of <a href="/wiki/West_Nile_virus" title="West Nile virus">West Nile virus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bronx_Park" title="Bronx Park">Bronx Park</a>, New York, involved northern bald ibises amongst many other species of birds and mammals.<sup id="cite_ref-ludwig_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ludwig-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe">Europe</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_bald_ibis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Europe">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>In 1504, a decree by <a href="/wiki/Leonhard_von_Keutschach" title="Leonhard von Keutschach">Archbishop Leonhard</a> of <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">Salzburg</a> made the northern bald ibis one of the world's earliest officially protected species. They nested in the cliffs and on castles and ruins in the Graz/Steiermark and Salzburg regions of Austria and vanished around 1630–1645.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Young birds were hunted as a delicacy at feasts for the nobility. Despite the decree, it died out in Austria as elsewhere in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-Shuker_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shuker-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg/220px-Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg/330px-Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg/440px-Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3888" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Graz_Schlossberg_Waldrapp_Infotafel.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Austrian reintroduction</div></div></div>
<p>There are now two ibis reintroduction projects in the Austria, at Grünau and <a href="/wiki/Kuchl" title="Kuchl">Kuchl</a>.<a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="http://waldrapp.eu/index.php/en/project-sites/breeding-area-kuchl">[1]</a> A research station at <a href="/wiki/Gr%C3%BCnau_im_Almtal" title="Grünau im Almtal">Grünau</a> has a breeding colony managed, like the Turkish population, as a free-flying flock which is caged at migration time. The aim here is to investigate flock interactions and hormonal status, behavioural and ecological aspects of natural foraging, and the establishment of traditions via social learning.<sup id="cite_ref-waza_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Scharnstein Project<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> is an attempt to establish a migratory <i>waldrapp</i> colony by using <a href="/wiki/Ultralight_aviation" title="Ultralight aviation">ultralight planes</a> to teach a migration route. The scheme builds on the Grünau research by developing a method to control and guide the autumn migration of a founder population, which then can pass this migration tradition to subsequent generations. In May 2002, 11 birds from the Vienna Zoo and the Grünau colony were trained to follow two microlight planes, and in 2003, a first attempt was made to lead a group of birds from <a href="/wiki/Scharnstein" title="Scharnstein">Scharnstein</a> to southern Tuscany. Due to adverse weather and technical problems, the birds had to be transported by road over a considerable part of the distance.<sup id="cite_ref-waza_64-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> The subsequent releases were more successful, with birds wintering in Tuscany, and, from 2005, returning to northern Austria. In 2008, a female ibis named Aurelia flew 930&#160;km (580&#160;mi) back to Austria for her fourth return to the breeding site. The hazards of the journey are shown by the loss of her two offspring and her mate while on the southern journey in the autumn of 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-Waldrapp_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Waldrapp-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg/220px-Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg/330px-Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg/440px-Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3456" data-file-height="4608" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Waldrapp_Voliere_Heiligenberg_20190714_HDR.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Waldrapp aviary near Lake Constance</div></div></div>
<p>In August 2013 the European Union agreed to provide support to reintroduction projects until 2019 under its <b>LIFE+ Biodiversity</b> programme.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The <i>Reason for Hope</i> project<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> under the leadership of the biologist Dr. Johannes Fritz has operated one breeding and observation site in Austria, in Kuchl, near Salzburg, and two similar sites in <a href="/wiki/Burghausen,_Alt%C3%B6tting" title="Burghausen, Altötting">Burghausen</a>, Bavaria, and in <a href="/wiki/%C3%9Cberlingen" title="Überlingen">Überlingen</a> on <a href="/wiki/Lake_Constance" title="Lake Constance">Lake Constance</a> in Baden-Württemberg.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The positions and flight patterns of migratory birds are monitored with light-weight solar transmitters. After learning to follow their human foster-mothers seated in ultralight aircraft, around 30 young birds are led over the Alps to spend the winter months in Tuscany.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> Numerous studies on migratory bird behaviour have been published and presentations given at symposiums.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>  In November 2019 it was announced that the project team succeeded in uniting juvenile birds with experienced adult birds so that they could fly to their wintering site together.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i>Proyecto Eremita</i> is a Spanish reintroduction involving the release of nearly 30 birds in the Ministry of Defence training ground in <a href="/wiki/La_Janda" title="La Janda">La Janda</a> district, <a href="/wiki/Barbate" title="Barbate">Barbate</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz_(province)" class="mw-redirect" title="Cádiz (province)">Cádiz Province</a>. It had its first success in 2008, when a pair laid two eggs. This is probably the first attempt to breed in the wild in Spain for 500 years as the last definite reference to the northern bald ibis breeding in Spain is from a 15th-century falconry book.<sup id="cite_ref-elpais_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elpais-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> This effort has been undertaken by the <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusian</a> government's Environmental Ministry, the Spanish Ministry of Defence, and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Zoobot%C3%A1nico_de_Jer%C3%A9z&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Zoobotánico de Jeréz (page does not exist)">Zoobotánico de Jeréz</a> (<a href="/wiki/Jerez_de_la_Frontera" title="Jerez de la Frontera">Jerez</a> Zoo and Botanical Gardens), with the assistance of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Estaci%C3%B3n_Biol%C3%B3gica_de_Do%C3%B1ana&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Estación Biológica de Doñana (page does not exist)">Doñana Biological Station</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_National_Research_Council" title="Spanish National Research Council">CSIC</a> and volunteers from the Cádiz Natural History Society.<sup id="cite_ref-elpais_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elpais-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Proyectoeremita_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Proyectoeremita-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-mde_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mde-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> Previously, two birds left the area in 2005 and 14 in 2006, but nothing is known of their whereabouts other than that a ringed bird from Spain was seen in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_Atlas" title="Middle Atlas">Middle Atlas</a>, Morocco in 2005. Internet pictures of this species taken near <a href="/wiki/Arma%C3%A7%C3%A3o_de_P%C3%AAra" title="Armação de Pêra">Armação de Pêra</a>, Algarve, Portugal in 2009 and later, may be related to those releases in Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-waza_64-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> In the interim, the Spanish colony has been growing very well, from 9 breeding pairs in 2011, 10 in 2012 and 15 in 2013 to 23 breeding pairs in 2014, which successfully raised 25 chicks in 2014 (<a href="/w/index.php?title=Quercus_349(2015):_14-23&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Quercus 349(2015): 14-23 (page does not exist)">Quercus 349(2015): 14-23</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> In 2014 the total population of this colony was 78 wild birds split into two colonies, originally along the cliffs of the Atlantic coast and in 2012 with a second colony of 5–6 breeding pairs that started at the cliffs 10&#160;km inland next to a country road at La Barca de Vejer (<a href="/wiki/Vejer_de_la_Frontera" title="Vejer de la Frontera">Vejer de la Frontera</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Northern_Morocco">Northern Morocco</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_bald_ibis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Northern Morocco">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg/220px-Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="186" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg/330px-Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg/440px-Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1095" data-file-height="925" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Atlas-Mountains-Labeled-2_new.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Location of the Rif mountains</div></div></div>
<p>There is a planned reintroduction of the ibis at Ain Tijja-<a href="/wiki/Mezguitem" class="mw-redirect" title="Mezguitem">Mezguitem</a> in the north-east of <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>. Since the wild populations further south remain vulnerable, and the porous sandstone of their breeding ledges is exposed to erosion, the intention is to establish a non-migratory population (stocked from German, Swiss, and Austrian zoos) in an area where this species was known to have bred up to about 1980. The station in the <a href="/wiki/Rif" title="Rif">Rif</a> mountains was built in 2000, and stocked with the first group of zoo-bred birds. A second importation of zoo-bred birds and the construction of an information centre took place in 2004. Six pairs bred in 2006 subsequent to a change in the birds' diet, and six offspring from five nests were successfully reared. In 2007 there were 19 birds (13 adults and six juveniles) in the aviary.<sup id="cite_ref-waza3_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza3-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The rock walls of the mountains have many potential breeding ledges, and an artificial lake provides water to the birds and to the local human population. Steppe pasture which is not exposed to herbicides or pesticides gives good foraging. Once the population reaches around 40 birds, a release will be initiated, subject to international agreement. The reintroduction site is 760&#160;km (470&#160;mi) from Agadir on the other side of the Atlas Mountains, so accidental contamination of the wild colonies is unlikely.<sup id="cite_ref-waza4_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-waza4-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_culture">In culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_bald_ibis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: In culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Akh_glyph.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Akh_glyph.svg/220px-Akh_glyph.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="199" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Akh_glyph.svg/330px-Akh_glyph.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Akh_glyph.svg/440px-Akh_glyph.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="267" data-file-height="242" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Akh_glyph.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Northern bald ibis in <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_hieroglyphs" title="Egyptian hieroglyphs">Egyptian hieroglyphs</a>.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_(M.A.N._Madrid)_06.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg/220px-Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="289" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg/330px-Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg/440px-Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_%28M.A.N._Madrid%29_06.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2087" data-file-height="2744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mosaico_Trabajos_H%C3%A9rcules_(M.A.N._Madrid)_06.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">Heracles</a> fights the Stymphalian birds</div></div></div>
<p>According to local legend in the <a href="/wiki/Birecik" title="Birecik">Birecik</a> area, the northern bald ibis was one of the first birds that <a href="/wiki/Noah" title="Noah">Noah</a> released from the <a href="/wiki/Noah%27s_Ark" title="Noah&#39;s Ark">Ark</a> as a symbol of fertility,<sup id="cite_ref-Shuker_68-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shuker-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> and a lingering religious sentiment in Turkey helped the colonies there to survive long after the demise of the species in Europe, as described above.<sup id="cite_ref-aewa6_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-aewa6-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>This ibis was revered as a holy bird and a symbol of brilliance and splendour in Ancient Egypt,<sup id="cite_ref-unep_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unep-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FAO_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAO-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> where, together with the <a href="/wiki/Sacred_ibis" class="mw-redirect" title="Sacred ibis">sacred ibis</a>, it was regarded as an embodiment of <a href="/wiki/Thoth" title="Thoth">Thoth</a>, scribe of the gods, who was usually depicted with a man's body and the head of an ibis. The <a href="/wiki/Old_Egyptian" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Egyptian">Old Egyptian</a> word <i>akh</i>, "to be resplendent, to shine", was denoted in <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_hieroglyphs" title="Egyptian hieroglyphs">hieroglyphs</a> by a bald ibis, presumably as a reference to its glossy plumage.<sup id="cite_ref-Lamy_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lamy-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> In a more abstract sense, <i>akh</i> stood for excellence, glory, honour, and virtue.<sup id="cite_ref-FAO_85-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FAO-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> It has also been used to signify the <a href="/wiki/Egyptian_soul" class="mw-redirect" title="Egyptian soul">soul</a> or spirit, one of five elements constituting personality.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Herodotus" title="Herodotus">Herodotus</a> wrote of the man-eating <a href="/wiki/Stymphalian_birds" title="Stymphalian birds">Stymphalian birds</a>, which had wings of brass and sharp metallic feathers they could fire at their victims. Ridding <a href="/wiki/Lake_Stymphalia" title="Lake Stymphalia">Lake Stymphalia</a> in <a href="/wiki/Arcadia" title="Arcadia">Arcadia</a> of these creatures was one of the twelve <a href="/wiki/Labours_of_Hercules" title="Labours of Hercules">labours of Heracles</a>. These mythical birds are sometimes considered to be based on the northern bald ibis,<sup id="cite_ref-Shuker_68-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shuker-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> but since they were described as marsh birds, and usually depicted without crests, the legendary species is more likely to be derived from the sacred ibis.<sup id="cite_ref-Hall_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hall-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Some depictions, such as the 6th-century BC Athenian black-figure amphora in the <a href="/wiki/British_Museum" title="British Museum">British Museum</a>, clearly show the black head and white body of the sacred ibis.<sup id="cite_ref-Britmus_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Britmus-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> After the bald ibis became extinct in Central Europe, some later writers thought that Gesner's description was one of several in his book depicting mythical creatures.<sup id="cite_ref-Shuker_68-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shuker-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Galler_542.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/St_Galler_542.jpg/220px-St_Galler_542.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/St_Galler_542.jpg/330px-St_Galler_542.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/St_Galler_542.jpg/440px-St_Galler_542.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1737" data-file-height="882" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:St_Galler_542.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Illumination in a manuscript from 1562 at <a href="/wiki/St._Gallen" title="St. Gallen">St. Gallen</a></div></div></div>
<p>The bird painted in 1490 in one of the <a href="/wiki/Gothic_fresco" class="mw-redirect" title="Gothic fresco">Gothic frescoes</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Trinity_Church,_Hrastovlje" class="mw-redirect" title="Holy Trinity Church, Hrastovlje">Holy Trinity Church in Hrastovlje</a> (now southwestern Slovenia) in the <a href="/wiki/Karst_Plateau" title="Karst Plateau">Karst</a> by <a href="/wiki/John_of_Kastav" title="John of Kastav">John of Kastav</a> was most probably the northern bald ibis.<sup id="cite_ref-PT2001_27-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PT2001-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> A small illustration of the northern bald ibis is found in the illuminated <i>St Galler Handschrift</i> of 1562,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> a drawing by <a href="/wiki/Joris_Hoefnagel" title="Joris Hoefnagel">Joris Hoefnagel</a> in <i>Missale Romanum</i> (1582-1590) and in paintings in the collection of Rudolf II at Vienna.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> It is believed that it had also been depicted at other places in <a href="/wiki/Istria" title="Istria">Istria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dalmatia" title="Dalmatia">Dalmatia</a>, where it was presumably native during the Middle Ages, e.g. in the local church in <a href="/wiki/Gradi%C5%A1%C4%8De_pri_Diva%C4%8Di" title="Gradišče pri Divači">Gradišče pri Divači</a> and in the coat of arms of the noble family Elio from <a href="/wiki/Koper" title="Koper">Koper</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The portal of <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lukovec_Castle&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lukovec Castle (page does not exist)">Lukovec Castle</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lukovica_pri_Brezovici" title="Lukovica pri Brezovici">Lukovica pri Brezovici</a> (central Slovenia) also features this species.<sup id="cite_ref-Delo66559_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Delo66559-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Birecik, Turkey an ancient celebration 'Kelaynak yortusu' held in mid-February to mark the return of the birds from Africa was revived in the 1950s.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_25-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Several countries have produced postage stamps which depict the northern bald ibis. They include Algeria, Morocco, Sudan, Syria, Turkey, and Yemen, which are breeding or migration locations; Austria, which is seeking to reintroduce the bird; and <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-dutton_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dutton-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup> which has a small captive population.<sup id="cite_ref-stamp_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stamp-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Further_reading">Further reading</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Northern_bald_ibis&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Further reading">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
